together knowe mare desyreth horse also many mare one stallion able couer one yeare fynallye stallion remoued cap v order obserued towchinge couerynge mare stallion run wyth theym pasture kepte stable stallion dieted also tyme day mare ought couered fynally knowe whether haue conceiued cap vi howe make mare conceiue either horse foles mare foles coloure luste haue selfe cap vii whether mare forced abide horse though haue luste howe make horse mare hauing lust haue luste engender also abate luste nede requyre cap viii whiche mare shoulde couered euerye yeare mare whiche would haue beare euerye appointed breedinge horse also groundes ought deuided ende deuision serueth cap fyrst towchinge ground twoo thinges considered quantitye qualitye quantitye twoo respectes first intent charged cattell able beare cattell sufficiently fedde prosper seconde respect greater ground particions nedefull partlye chaūge pasture sake according olde prouerbe chaunge pasture maketh fatte calues particions wolde made high pale rayle el depe ditche verye thicke quicke set horse mare wilde coltes easelye kepte cattel chiefely particions nedeful aswell stallion run euery one seuerally selfe together owne mare time engendring also coltes weanynge time commes seuered dammes whiche twoo pointes shall speake hereafter due place large moreouer suche particions besides comoditie grasse haye shall preserued thereby winter store grounde selfe parhaps ample waste wilde thereby enclininge cattell lyke nature shalbe brought formality beastes selues shall made domesticall famylyar rather yf handeled made tame youth whereof shall talke hereafter large notwithstanding would haue ground straitened particions maye haue sufficyent scope run trauell fro therin lyuing much labour leanes pouerty depryueth lust engēder euen ouermuch rest fatnes letteth conception causeth daungerous folyng wherefore would wyshe mare kepte meane estate vntill haue foled best fedde intent may haue aboundance mylke dugges whiche matter shalbe talked hereafter full proper place appoynt howe many acre ground serue mare ofspringe vntill mete broken thinke nedefull sith goodnesse ground must rule matter partlye discrecion owner experiens ought knowe owne ground beste groundes like fertilitye neither thinke owner ignoraunt knoweth horse mare greater feader kinde cattell therfore nede haue greater allowance yet consideringe horse biteth nerer ground cattell shepe cony onlye excepted whereby gathereth foode one acre ground beast almost acre halfe thinkes thirde parte wyll serue cowe ofspringe shoulde also feede mare ofspringe well prouided winter season hard meate hard cattell reason haue sharper teth bothe chowe also swalowe downe meate spede therefore winter meate nede haue double allowaunce suche wynter meate mare coltes wolde bee good sweete hay wel stacked vp dryeste warmest place ground wintered nyghe vnto stackes would built howses mete harber well mare theyr foles weanlynges seuerally feruēt heat stoned horse haue cannot consume much meate chiefly perhaps gueldings easy rule waye horse thus hauing sufficiently talked diuers kindes horse mare whiche metest realme aswell generall moste parte engender hys lyke aswell condicions shape body requysite therefore wold haue good race circumspect chosing first stallion mare woulde haue race discend intent maye reape therof pleasure grysons opinion sufficientlye treated booke arte rydinge shall nede therefore nowe trouble many wordes onelye make briefe resital al color best browne bay dapple gray bright bay rone white lyard pure black whyte starre foreheade wyse let stallion al one colour cleare bright pyed diuers colour albeit haue white blacke marke place conueniente bewtifull haue white starre forehead outermost partes body blacke tippes eares mayne tayle el feete white accordinge colour doeth properly require thing haue talked large booke ridyng towching hys shape woulde sort let haue short slender heade wyde mouth wyde nosethriels slender iawes great eye blacke boulting outwarde hollow inwarde short eares sharpe poynted like mouse necke rather long shorte greate towardes breast slender towardes heade creast wherof would rysyng middes therwith neither thick thin hauing crispe main hanging naturally ryght syde brode brest full apparaunt muscle brawnes fleshe also brode shoulder large bulke gaunt belly straight sharpe poynted wythers short playne backe great round buttockes long busshye tayle yard stone meane syse one stone hanging sider another trussed vppe rounde together large thighes long hawnches behynd stronge legges great iointes aswell befor behind short pastournes longe fewterlockes also rounde smouth blacke harde hollow sounding houes finally let hys whole body together haue roundenes according length pointes well proporcioned may seme high stature stronge lym also liuelye eye thus much shape goodnes hys goodnes may partly naturall partly artificiall neither throughly knowen doynges naturall goodnesse chiefly consisteth healthfulnes body aboundaunce good seade strength agilitie swiftnes good disposition aptenes taught yea pace galloppinge runninge bearinge heade eares thinges may also much holpen art reyne well beare heade steaddely ready tourne lyght stoppe handle feete orderlye kepe grounde obey rider assayes proceadeth rather art nature artificiall goodnes whether hath booke rydinge doth playnely teach iudge albeit stallion whiche chieflye serue couer mare artificiall goodnes materiall naturall good thinges mentioned amongest one chiefe point yet cannot perfectly knowen onles might se couer mare wete whether seade good time maye verye well bee knowen sort take betwixte thombe finger locke woll fealing towsyng woll semeth fyrme faste slymye good ouer lyquyd waterishe naught horse slowe couering doth liuely spirite courage hath one stone gret wartes growing stone haue naturally whyte specke eye mete stallion coltes shall begette haue lyke defectes wherefore nigh let stallion without al fault towching age stallion althoughe men oure dayes make matter thereof may get foles vntill xx xxx yeares olde yea long lyueth holpen therefore moste place realme appoynt horse vse suche verye olde therwith parhaps lame blynde yet men olde time made great matter thereof allowed stallion good v yeres xiiii affirming one perfect thing doth bryng forth another perfect vnperfect bringeth forth lyke horse accompted vnperfect vntil v yeares old iointes tyme throughly knitte neyther growen full strength xiiii yeares beginneth againe waxe vnperfect nature hym tyme sore decaied insomuch decrepit age death selfe nature doth shortely folowe albeit wyll denye good kepynge stronge complexion may cause one horse continue lust courage much longer nother albertus writeth knewe souldiour serued fielde horse lxx yeare olde yet compted able horse niphus also saieth emperour ferdynandus fyrst hys stable horse lxx yeares old self haue sene stallion haue ben xx yeares old aboue haue gotten vere fayre coltes eye yet beleue lyke perfection stallion might haue gotten lustye age coltes olde stallion moste parte dull slowe haue tender hofes subiecte hardening houes shall talke thereof come treate disease horse ¶how know stature making disposition foles new foled come age cap xiiii foles haue verye long legges euen birth proue commonly tal stature maneges ¶of maneging many kindes maneges cap xx italion word maneggiare much say englishe handle skill saye handle horse weapon verye well amongest italions taken generall word comprehendinge foure especiall kindes maneginge wherof one make horse double tournes call raddopiare make gallop fielde goyng skirremishe thirde make leape loft fetch diuers saultes fourth pace trot galloppe good fro one selfe path length xx xxx pace turning eche ende therof eyther single turne whole turne double turne grison calleth maneggiare repolom englishe menne call laste kinde manege absolutely without addicion amongst horseman word manege maneging signifieth none thinge onlye foresayde kinde gallopping turning fro one selfe path therfore vse commonly say horse canne manege well make good manege whereof also thre kindes saye manege haulfe rest manege whole rest manege without rest grison termeth thus manegio mezzo tempo tempo contra tempo manege halfe rest cause horse ende euerye maneging path hath stopt aduaunce twyse together seconde bounde tourne wherby rest alwayes one bound manege whole reste turne thyrde bounde reste two boundes manage without reste tourne hym immediatly vpon stoppe without tarriaunce whyche onelye kynde manege englyshe ryders commonlie vse thother two notwithstanding verye necessarye mete vsed accordinge horse stronge weake verye strong horse requireth manege wyth hole rest horse indifferent strength manege haulfe rest weake horse manege without rest manege haulfe rest necessary best meane make horse perfyght thother two note al iii kindes maneges must obserue well generall preceptes gaue touchinge single double tournes see horse kepe alwayes one path one place stoppe tourninge kepe hys ground carie head necke leg whole body orderly without preasing forward passe swyft cariere cap xxvi vntill youre horse perfect poyntes taught specially stop well therwith aduaunce aswel trot gallop woulde wyshe wyse run hym vnlesse beginning breakinge geue cariere two know swyftnes disposition leaue vntil better broken made mete run whan shall vse order folowinge ryde fayre playne sandy way voyde al stumbling stone acquaint waye pace faire softly length good cariere must measured according horse made mightye puissaunt horse great stature cariere would shorter likewise must wold haue bound aloft cariere made lyke iennet middle stature cariere path maye longer yet ouerlong thende whereof let hym stop aduaunce seconde bounde turne hym faire softly right hand stay litle sodenly saying liuely voice hey put forward spurres forcing al way run swiftlye roundlye possiblye euen thende thintent may stop buttockes done tourne left hand pace foorth faire softlye vnto thother ende cariere path stop turne right hand dyd leaue note chiefest poyntes obserued running cariere first see horse gather roundlye go smoothlye awaye bearyng head stedely secondly runne swiftlye thirdlye stop lightlye whereunto shall bring meanes wel often vsyng tread rynges swyft trot shall make hym nymble legges swyfte staide heade cometh afterward bee run shalbe griefe vnto hym whiche well obserued great rider cola pagano vntil sawe horse well stayde heade throughlye broken woulde neuer run spent foure monethes halfe yere yea perchaunce whole yeare breaking order haue heretofore taught woulde teache run lesse viii dayes swyftlye smoothlye stronglye stedines head lightnes stoppe could amended yea woulde haue horse texcell verie fine deede woulde teach nothinge beginninge thending shoulde first perfectlye well vpon soft pace vpon trot seldome neuer vpon gallop vnlesse necessity forced aboue al thing would sure neuer manege hym swift gallop yet make passe cariere sawe perfect rest would appoint ryder coulde require nothing horse redy manege single tourne double
